<Rate>5</Rate>< Text>
There are some amazing trails with beautiful views around Trojan Point. One trail leads to an awesome stone bench memorial at the top of a hill with a beautiful view of the ocean, the mountains, the bay, and the cities. There's also a rope swing and you feel like you're flying off the mountain into the sea, it's incredible!</Text>

I liked the price but I hesitated to reserve sight unseen. So I went to the location and asked to see a 10 x 16 space. First I was shown a 10 x 20 space with a very low ceiling, first floor. I asked if there was anything else and was shown a 10 x 16 in a separate bldg which had higher ceilings, so square footage doesn't reflect real size. The second issue is that the price will bump back to the original fee of over 400. oo in 300 days kind of like a bad heal estate desalt where suddenly its completely unaffordable. I liked the 2nd unit, ask to hold it but was told I couldn't hold for the online price: "go home and reserve there'. So I went home, located the space and tried reserving only to have some erroneous response of "unit unavailable" listed. Fine. I returned with confirmation in hand. They begin processing, meaning I have to fill in all of my information on a touchscreen. < review>
I shopped online and around our county for a month before I discovered Far Below Retail and I will not being buying furniture from anyone else but them. The quality of workmanship, the helpfulness of staff, and the prices cannot be beat. On the furniture I selected, the lowest price I could find elsewhere was still 75% higher - I saved over $10K buying from them. The delivery team was on time, focused, quick, and cleaned up after themselves. We have been living with our new furniture for two months now and I couldn't be happier!

We bought a custom made sofa, love seat, and a bedroom set. There was a showroom version of the sofa, there were hundreds of colors and fabrics to choose from, and Dave was so helpful with helping me to decide an awesome combination for my beach/modern minimalist style. Although they did not have a model on the floor of bed I wanted, Dave was very helpful in showing me catalog in store and URL on website for what he thought I might like so then I only had to choose from 3 rather than the thousands that they have - I selected a dark cherry bedroom set of a higher platform bed with matching nightstand and dresser which could have all been bought separately. The bed even has three level touch lights under the bed at your fingertips so you can find your way to bathroom without stumbling in middle of night - sweet! I also had designers I liked for other furniture and Dave said to just let him know who and what pieces and he emailed back the next day with prices for all of them, some less than the advertised price at those designer's own website.</review>

<Review>I have copied and pasted this review from 2011 from Yelp. It is interesting for me to notice that Yelp filtered out this review and almost all the other 1 star reviews.

AVOID!

We drove here based on the fantastic YELP reviews, but now suspect these reviews were done by family and friends.

The employees were very nice and helpful, but misrepresented an item, though probably not intentionally. After getting it home we found that they sold us the wrong color. We had to repack it and drive it all the way back. Not a problem, mistakes happen. But they charged a 20% restocking fee for a cash and carry item (it was in stock, we didn't special order it) which was THEIR mistake.

In addition, the person handling the return was incredibly rude and somewhat violent. Because we did not want to agree to have the restocking fee subtracted from our refund, he started yelling and said he wasn't taking it back and actually pushed the item outside.

Because my husband and I do not live in California (we were there helping my son move) we were not at all familiar with furniture stores in that area. In searching online, we discovered Yelp reviews, and Far Below Retail has reviews that sounded almost too good to be true. Guess they were. As long as I am editing this review, I may as well include a paragraph from one of my emails to Christina:

"Christina, I don't enjoy writing a bad review. The misrepresentation (even if inadvertent) cost us valuable time, effort, and gasoline, but that is not why I wrote the review. We felt the restocking fee was unfair because it was a cash and carry item that was not special ordered, and the color was misrepresented., but that would still not be enough for me to write a bad review. I wrote the review after my husband and son came home visibly shaken from the return experience."

Do yourself a favor and avoid this unprofessional operation. Buy your furniture from a reputable dealer instead.< /Review><name>Lori Hise</name><user_id>117158240160472720782</user_id></record>

< Review>
Dr. Ferrick and his staff are amazing. I had anxiety about going to the dentist and even avoided going for years. I was afraid of the amount of work needed, the judgement, and the shots! Earlier this year, I experienced some discomfort with my tooth and chose to see Dr. Ferrick for his expertise in nervous patients. His staff was able to fit me in the same week right before he left on vacation. At my first visit, he explained everything to me and worked with me to get this dental work done with another doctor while he was gone on vacation. He even met with the other doctor and gave instructions to handle my anxiety carefully. I had to take anti-anxiety medication before my appointments. From then on, I've been seeing Dr. Ferrick regularly and no longer needing medication. I've been going to his office for months (4+ visits) now to make up for those many years not seeing a dentist but I'm so happy to found a dentist to stick with and knows me so well. HIs staff are very kind and responsive. I highly recommend Dr. Ferrick and his staff for any patients but especially a nervous patient like me who was scared of dental work and the judgement!< /Review>

<review>The only word I can think of that accurately describes Watermark is "incompetent".

I initially contacted them in July of 2020 regarding a very straightforward refinance of my primary residence. The rate they offered was very good, so I immediately provided them with all required documentation to lock it in and shortly thereafter is when I encountered issue after issue...after issue.

First, was a complete lack of communication. Literally over a month passed at one point with not even a peep from them. When they would come out of the wood work, it was to request the same documents that I had already sent them - this happened multiple times. Really frustrating.

Then, when I finally thought they had their act together, they sent me updated disclosures and FINALLY provided a closing date. That date came and went with literally zero communication from anyone. I wrote them off at that point, but then...

Another month passed and they come out of the blue, yet again with updated disclosures that looked good, so I decided to give them another shot. A closing date and time was scheduled (again) and after scheduling my neighbor to come by to witness the signing and leaving my son's baseball practice early, I get a call from the closing attorney 15 minutes before the scheduled closing: no documents. Watermark failed to provide the closing documents to the attorney. Unbelievable.

Needless to say, I've now permanently blacklisted Watermark and refuse to do business with them both now and in the future. I've never in my life been jerked around so much by a company.

This experience might have actually been a blessing in disguise though because I've read that Watermark services some of their own loans. I can only imagine how awful that must be for their customers who are stuck dealing with them for years and decades on end. That said, I'll happily pay a half point more to work with a competent company who doesn't frustrate the daylights out of me at every turn.

Good riddance, Watermark!< /review></record></dataset><record>

<Text>Ok, this is an interesting company to work with. The review is long and contains very useful information for anyone who is thinking of using this company for their mortgage needs.
I worked with Watermark back in 2015-16 to refinance my home, that time I did not have any issue and the transaction was smooth from start to finish.
Since then I have had two mortgages with Watermark. One day in March 2020 I received an email from Watermark to apply for refinance with NO Closing Cost. I replied to that email and asked what options are available (15yr & 30yr). I never received a response for that email but a few weeks later I received another email that is asking me to sign up for an account for recent application submitted and to review "Pre Disclosure". I reached out to the agent who contacted me through email for refinance but he never responded. After receiving more emails about creating account and continuing the process of application, one day, I received a letter in mail stating that my credit score and report has been obtained by Watermark and they will use this credit report to make decision on my application. WATERMARK CHECKED MY CREDIT WITHOUT MY CONSENT. In reality I never applied for refinance and Watermark has already started my application to refi. I reached out to the agent by phone and email but he never responded. After few more days I decided to call their Irvine office and talk to his supervisor. I spoke to his supervisor and told the whole story - first he was thinking that I am a bogus customer but later after looking into my "submitted application" he realized that my first application from 2016 was resubmitted with same loan amount (which is over 100k higher than correct amount). He then offered me refinance with current loan amount and low interest rate and no closing cost. When I created new application as per his instructions, I was NOT offered "NO COST" refi but the cost was over $5000.00 including existing HELOC subordination fee. Fine, the process started but it grew painful by the time, their system does not understand password protected pdfs so I had to email sensitive files. After two months of back and forth I decided to refi my other home which is a rental single family home. I was offered slightly higher APR as it was an investment property - it was definitely lower than current APR tho. While they were working on my primary home refi they contacted HELOC provider and failed to strike a deal that forced me to either obtain an inspection or sign "Voluntary Suspension of Line". Before signing this document and tried to convince Watermark to waive the cost of inspection but the response from the loan office was "What?? you want me pay for inspection?"(sic). And I was also told that if I do not either spend money to get my own inspection or sign that document the deal will fall apart and refi will not happen. I had to sign the document since I was already trapped by Watermark. In July I was informed about closing and was told to schedule time for document signup with a Notary. The first scheduled time no one showed up so we setup another time next week. This time the notary showed up and we spent about 1.5 hours signing up closing documents. After signing was done I was told I will be contacted by the company again for closing refi on other house. Two weeks later I received a call to schedule another appointment with a Notary for closing, we scheduled a day and time for the same. When Notary arrived I was shocked to see that she had paperwork for both the houses - we did not know what to do. I showed her a copy of the closing documents that I already signed a couple of weeks ago. We then reached out to Watermark to see what this drama is, then I was told that the previous closing did not happen and they "thought" that I was informed by "someone" at Watermark. Fine.. I again signed up the closing document and this time it was properly closed.

Monica Reyes was fantastic--gave us daily updates on the interest rate until we were ready to lock, was up-front with everything. <user_name>Ella Minnow Pea</user_name><time>1594491268263</time><Rate>1<//Rate>< review>
Fairly disappointing high pressure / low service mortgage broker. Initial conversations included veiled threats that "mortgage rates won't be this low again" - they were and, after closing, are even lower. Instead of honest discussions about what I was being told by other brokers, they just insisted that I didn't understand what was being offered. The broker insisted my application wouldn't target a hard credit pull, which was a lie. I should have switched brokers at that point, but once you start the paperwork process, it's hard to walk away knowing they have all your personal information.

The process took 57 days on a very simple refinance from lock to funding and I only found out everything was okay by receiving a system generated email after funding. During processing and underwriting, there was rarely communication or movement without me prodding. If you use them, I'd suggest calling every day to make sure things are moving. When I did contact them, the responses were often inaccurate or unrelated to my question. They sent me someone else's tax return at one point because they mixed me up with someone else. I indicated that I wanted to pay closing costs out of pocket, but they rolled them into the loan and didn't respond to my emails asking about it. Perhaps their commissions are based on loan values. The closing disclosures weren't accurate and the signing was done with a notary who didn't have specific information on my file so asking questions wasn't an option without creating further delays. There were numerous other small issues along the way. The refinance did complete, but I wouldn't work with them again after the experience.</review>

<user>107743080632133824312<//user><Name>Scott Jensen<//Name>< Time>

<Rate>1</Rate>< text>
Trying to interact with Watermark on a home refinance was like unknowing being drug into the Pit of Dispair in The Princess Bride. Each week was a new, creative torture seemingly designed to suck years off of my life. I would hope I am a considerate person who recognizes when circumstances are out of someone's control and act reasonably. I also like to think I focus on the positive, giving people the benefit of the doubt and even praising my local DMV recently when the experience went really, really well. That said when a company seems to have little regard for someone's time or money I think it is also reasonable to let others know to be aware. With the recent record-low mortgage rates I applied through Watermark for a refinance on my home. I tend to be well organized and had all of my paperwork in order and went through the initial process in less than 30 minutes. I was contacted by a Watermark representative, who I don't think is fair to name here as he seemed to be following company policy rather than his own direction, to confirm my information and tell me they were experiencing a high volume of applications on so this might take a few weeks. I understood and followed up each week to see if they needed anything more from me. Each week I was assured all was well and that my loan would be reviewed shortly. After four weeks I was told my loan was moving forward and I needed to arrange for a home appraisal. I chose to use one of the companies Watermark recommended, arranged and paid the $400 for the appraisal. I did not hear back from Watermark after I received confirmation of the appraisal and followed up a week later. I was again told all was fine with the loan process but underwriting was backed up and my loan was delayed. I followed up again the following week and was given the same response. On the seventh week since submitting my application and "locking in my rate" I followed up again. I did not receive an immediate response. The following day I was sent an email informing me Watermark was no longer willing to process my refinance unless I paid an additional $2000 to continue the process. This is in addition to the fees they are taking to process the loan.If they had told me 2-3 weeks earlier I could have adjusted and moved to another company but mortgage rates had climbed again and I would not be able to lock in a rate that made sense to refinance. It feels like a scam and a big company trying to hold an individual hostage after striking them along.I told Watermark I no longer wanted to move forward with them and I would like a refund for the home inspection I paid for under their advice all was moving forward. They told me to pound sand. I feel like I was reasonable in asking for additional consideration considering the circumstances and received the same reply that if I wanted to move forward they would be happy to process my loan but that I needed to pay the additional $2000 but they would not refund me for the home inspection. After being drug along I choose to cut my losses but thought you should understand this companies business practices and decide if you want to risk being tortured by the six fingers man.
Anigo Montoya(Scott J.)</text>

< Review>
My refinance went very well.  Overall a fast process comparatively speaking, without any hassle of ever having to leave the house.  Start to finish less than a month, and it was done, which is terrific.  Very good interest rates, though higher than typical closing costs...but the low rates offset the higher closing costs.  They offered the best rates I could find anywhere.  There was a certain amount of duplication involved...we would send requested paperwork, then 3 days later they would ask for the same paperwork again...so we would simply send it again.  At times it seemed the left hand didn't know what the right hand was doing and they were a bit disorganized between the different assistants who were helping with various aspects of the job.  Otherwise it was not terrible and didn't cause any undue stress...but probably an extra 1/2 hour to hour of additional fiddling around on the computer that was entirely unnecessary.    FYI before I have even made my first payment, they sold my mortgage to another company...this is not a complaint, just a statement of fact.  It is common in the industry.  But if something like that might bother you, look elsewhere.  I frankly don't care that they sold my mortgage immediately as it doesn't impact me, just a little surprising it happened less than 3 weeks after closing!  Overall I would recommend them.  Casey was very responsive and helpful thru the entire process, and I have only those few small complaints about duplication of effort that prevented the 5 star rating they otherwise could have earned.<//Review>

My experience with Watermark Home Loans on my refi w/cashout was stress free - despite the Chrismas and New Year Holdays.  Thomas Cross was my Mortgage Banker.  He was extremely polite and patient.  For a week before Christmas, I emailed my questions and Mr Cross, without skipping a beat, responded with clarity.  If I didn't understand something, he would politely explain. <Review>Avoid Watermark loans at all costs!! Especially Martin C Franco & Mike Greenberg.

My wife and I were purchasing our first home and shopped around for an interest rate on a Jumbo ~1m+ loan for beach cities townhome. Although our real estate agent recommended other lenders, Watermark came back with a competitive rate and were prompt to get us the pre-approval letter - a decision we later regretted.

Things seemed to be going well for the first two weeks of the 30 day close, until Martin dropped a laundry list of 'outstanding' items that he still needed even though he had previously confirmed all the documentation was uploaded. Annoying, but not a huge problem. We promptly uploaded the documentation after several back and forths / technical difficulties with their upload server.

So we are two weeks out from close and I ask Martin to confirm we are all on track to meet the closing date. He promptly replies yes - no worries.

A day passes and he asks for $250 fee that needs to get paid to the 'HOA' for them to fill out a questionnaire. He states 'This is handled by escrow, but they want us to do it', which we thought was weird and we were not expecting this but filled out the credit card form for Watermark.
The next day we receive the loan disclosures and it clearly states that only $150 is needed for the HOA fee, so we have to go through an entire series of communication to get our $100 back ... painful, but not a huge deal in the scheme of things.

But then the fun begins. Note it was 10 days before closing and we thought we were all good as confirmed by Martin. Then the week we are supposed to close he calls and says we are going to miss the closing date because the 'HOA questionnaire' is not complete. This is the same questionnaire that we had just paid $150 for two weeks prior. Maybe it was a bad assumption that this would 'get done', but either way we had paid Watermark to get this done and they had failed to do so.

So we worked with our real estate agent to move out the close date. Initially Watermark said it would only be a day or two, but it ended up being an entire week.

On top of all of this, they said it was going to cost an extra $3100 (.36% of the loan) due to them missing the closing date. I fought this tooth and nail since the delay was directly their fault, but it was pretty clear when I got on the phone with Martin's boss Mike that this was how Watermark turns a profit - by ripping off their customers.

Lots of lessons learned from our first house purchase - hopefully this review will help save someone the stress and money of dealing with Watermark.<//Review>< user>

Ron and Genelle were both great to work with! Ron was the most transparent and educating mortgage banker that I "interviewed" in my search and, as a first-time home buyer, I needed both of those qualities in a lender. In our first conversation he did not assume that I already knew everything about the mortgage process, like others did; instead, he patiently and thoroughly explained details like:
--what is and is not included in closing costs
--what points are, and how both points and lender credits are acquired and affect your interest rate

Ron was always quick to respond to emails and, early on, told me to let him know if any concerns came up. My realtor did raise a concern with a past transaction he'd had with Watermark so I shared that concern with Ron and, while the transaction was not one of his, he acknowledged the concern and sought out some background. Genelle, my loan processor, has some great project management skills! She provided a clear list of the items I needed for underwriting, frequently checked in on progress, and quickly answer my questions.

It can be a bit tricky working with folks in opposite time zones (I'm on ET while Watermark is on PT), but Ron and Genelle were pleasant and professional and we closed on schedule and that's what matters in the end!<//Text>

<text>I see a lot of good reviews on here, but I notice that most of them are for refinances, which tend to be lower risk than first-time mortgages (because the person has already qualified for a mortgage in the past).

I made the mistake of trusting watermark and the loan officer, Kory Mathys, for the loan on my first home. I was told that the poor reviews on here were only from people who didn't submit the requested documents on time, and that he could easily secure my loan before closing of the 30 day escrow.

I had been rate shopping for loans for weeks and the best I could find for the condo we were buying was 4.65%
Kory told me he could get me 4.375%
The union bank loan officer told me that sounded "too good to be true" and that "online banks are known for not delivering." He would probably say "I told you so!" if he spoke to me now, because he was right.

Despite having great credit scores, very little debt, and sending every document I was asked for promptly, they ended up screwing me over. Everything was moving smoothly until the day before I had to remove contingencies from my purchase contract, when I was informed they would not be able to approve my loan. Kory told me to the bitter end that "technically" I had indeed been approved but that I just "couldn't satisfy the conditions." Well that is just double speak, either you're approved or you're not... if the conditions weren't satisfied then I wasn't approved, period. If I had trust him and removed the contingencies,  I would have lost my $8000 deposit and the house as well once the financing had fallen through.

I know I'm a reliable borrower, and the proof is in the pudding, as I ended up getting a loan with a different bank (with a slightly higher interest rate of 4.65% on the loan) and there was no issue with the underwriting in this case. I'm fortunate that I was able to have family lend me money to close on the deal and then secure my loan after the fact. Otherwise, I would have had cancel the contract and would have lost the money from the home inspection and the appraisal, which was almost $1000.

Be wary of a deal that seems too good to be true. To quote Mark Twain, "A banker is a fellow who lends you his umbrella when the sun is shining, but wants it back the minute it begins to rain."

Watermark made a big mistake with their dishonesty and lack of transparency. As a physician, my earning potential in the future is high, and I will never use watermark in the future and I will be sure to tell all my colleagues to avoid them as well.</text><Pictures>None</Pictures>< response>
